<div id="review_3101964726" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3101964726" />
    <a title="Irene" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36459924-irene"><img alt="Irene" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589091840p2/36459924.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3101964726?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irene" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irene" href="/user/show/36459924-irene">Irene</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/9285319-tales-from-earthsea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36459924-irene?shelf=fantasies-similar-to-earthsea">fantasies-similar-to-earthsea</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3101964726" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10350876409096854532">Read Earthsea in the order that Ursula K. Le Guin recommended. You may think that the short stories are an addendum to the overall Earthsea narrative but Le Guin had a reading order in mind. I say this because I was debating about whether to skip this one and move right into The Other Wind but I'm glad I didn't. Also, one of the stories is a bridge between Tehanu and The Other Wind. <br/><br/>In the Foreword, it sounded as though Le Guin couldn't force it in herself to write the fifth Earthsea novel as a </span>
  <span id="freeText10350876409096854532" style="display:none">Read Earthsea in the order that Ursula K. Le Guin recommended. You may think that the short stories are an addendum to the overall Earthsea narrative but Le Guin had a reading order in mind. I say this because I was debating about whether to skip this one and move right into The Other Wind but I'm glad I didn't. Also, one of the stories is a bridge between Tehanu and The Other Wind. <br /><br />In the Foreword, it sounded as though Le Guin couldn't force it in herself to write the fifth Earthsea novel as a full-length story."The Finder" could have been a full-length story. In fact, it's about 100 pages or so short if we take a general look at the length of other Earthsea novels. It also feels like it could have been a proper novel because "The Finder" is the strongest out of all the tales in terms of the strength of its storytelling. It is badass epic, it's got a love story *and* you learn about how the magic school on Roke was founded! The dark age of Earthsea is terrifying but wonderful all at the same time. <br /><br />"Darkrose and Diamond" was a lovely love story about a merchant's son who falls in love with a witch's daughter. It was a nice look at the mercantile class of Earthsea and how they perceived magic. It's not going to make your heart soar but it's a very sweet story. I personally would have loved if the merchant's son was a bit of a snob to create some tension in the relationship but that's the romantic reader in me... <br /><br />"The Bones of the Earth" is a look at Ogion and his teacher, Dulse. It is another amazing story that reveals some things that you didn't know but now that you know it's like a fun little easter egg. Also, a cute goat joke. The scene when Ogion brings up goats with Dulse is hilarious.<br /><br />What I loved most about Tales From Earthsea was that it explored the wizards that misbehaved. The misfits. The drop-outs. The ones not destined to save the world but perhaps save themselves and a little corner somewhere. Like, YES. And now that I think about it, there's got to be Earthsea fanfiction somewhere with more wizard, witch and sorcerer love stories. <br /><br />"On the High Marsh" was a surprisingly moving love story about the redemption of a bad wizard that takes place during the time Ged is Archmage. It's also an interesting look at a small cowboy town in Earthsea. It's not actually a cowboy town but the whole atmosphere of it is a small cattle town. The ending to the story is so powerful and touching - you feel so happy that Emer and Irioth have and found each other. The relationship between Emer and Irioth have a hint of older Ged and Tenar in there. <br /><br />"Dragonfly" is about Irian, a character we will meet again in The Other Wind. This is a really cool look at crumbling noble houses, but also of renegade wizards. Le Guin says "The Finder" came out of her interest to explore wizard celibacy and I think "Dragonfly" does a really good job at looking at wizards who took one look at what they were signing up for and was like, nope. Imma do a con over here. <br /><br />In Earthsea, Le Guin proves she's got the chemistry formula down pat for arrogant, powerful man meets haughty witch-like woman he doesn't particularly like but still wants to win over. That sketch of Ged as a kid meeting Serret, the Lord of Re Albi's daughter is so slight but it's so remarkable and unforgettable. To be fair, Le Guin is more skillful than some popular romance novelists at creating romantic chemistry. <br /><br />In "Dragonfly" we get again a glimpse of the wizard who wants to win a woman he doesn't really respect. Ivory playing his game over Irian was memorable but then the story soon switches to Epic Stuff when Ivory and Irian make their way to Roke. As "Dragonfly" can be considered a prequel of sorts to The Other Wind, the final book of Earthsea will be that much more meaningful if you have read "Dragonfly." It won't take away from the finale of The Other Wind but you'll get more hints of where we are going, you'll also get and love Irian more too.<br /><br />Wouldn't it have been grand if there were like 50 more Tales from Earthsea? Ursula K. Le Guin was an amazing author and her words live on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10350876409096854532" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_340592370" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/340592370" />
    <a title="R. Scot Johns" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1827100-r-scot-johns"><img alt="R. Scot Johns" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442495004p2/1827100.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/340592370?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R. Scot Johns" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R. Scot Johns" href="/user/show/1827100-r-scot-johns">R. Scot Johns</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1827100-r-scot-johns?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1827100-r-scot-johns?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer340592370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4921078723060143084">The more I read Le Guin the less I like her writing. She has no sense of pacing or plotting whatsoever, leaving the single "event" of each book or story until the last few pages, reached only after a slow and tedious preamble in which the characters sit around doing nothing (as if that's a plot point or an action of its own), and somehow we're supposed to identify with them in their non-quest for nothing. Some of her characters show promise, but we never see it come to true fruition.<br/><br/>I appreciate</span>
  <span id="freeText4921078723060143084" style="display:none">The more I read Le Guin the less I like her writing. She has no sense of pacing or plotting whatsoever, leaving the single "event" of each book or story until the last few pages, reached only after a slow and tedious preamble in which the characters sit around doing nothing (as if that's a plot point or an action of its own), and somehow we're supposed to identify with them in their non-quest for nothing. Some of her characters show promise, but we never see it come to true fruition.<br /><br />I appreciate her Taoist outlook, but the Tao is not an anti-action philosophy, it is not one of sitting immobile waiting for something to happen to you, but one of movement and motion with the flow of the world around one, of graceful action in concert with the natural order. Reading itself is an action, an event, the turning of each page a change from what has been into a realm of what is possible to become. Le Guin is satisfied with simply leaving what is as it is and describing it. What happens at the end is thrown in almost as an afterthought, as a way of saying that she's finished writing for now.<br /><br />This collection of five short stories also exemplifies perfectly the reason I so dislike short fiction. There is no time to develop characters (not that she really ever does that in her longer works), or get to know them or their motivations. There is only a hint of promise, left unfulfilled.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4921078723060143084" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review340592370">
  <td colspan="2">
    <div class="updateActionLinks">

<div id="review_2519781793" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2519781793" />

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2519781793" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer4663536666013910910">This is a collection of short stories set in Earthsea universe. They span the period from several centuries prior to the first volume <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13642.A_Wizard_of_Earthsea__Earthsea_Cycle___1_' title='A Wizard of Earthsea (Earthsea Cycle, #1) by Ursula K. Le Guin' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Wizard of Earthsea</a> to years after the fourth <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13661.Tehanu__Earthsea_Cycle___4_' title='Tehanu (Earthsea Cycle, #4) by Ursula K. Le Guin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tehanu</a>.<br/>This is the unique feature of SFF that if desired, you may get answers even to questions you haven’t initially even thought to ask. I’m sure that when Le Guin was writing <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13642.A_Wizard_of_Earthsea__Earthsea_Cycle___1_' title='A Wizard of Earthsea (Earthsea Cycle, #1) by Ursula K. Le Guin' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Wizard of Earthsea</a>, she just based the mage academy on Roke island on ‘classical’ European university, were both the faculty and pupils wer</span>
  <span id="freeText4663536666013910910" style="display:none">This is a collection of short stories set in Earthsea universe. They span the period from several centuries prior to the first volume <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13642.A_Wizard_of_Earthsea__Earthsea_Cycle___1_" title="A Wizard of Earthsea (Earthsea Cycle, #1) by Ursula K. Le Guin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Wizard of Earthsea</a> to years after the fourth <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13661.Tehanu__Earthsea_Cycle___4_" title="Tehanu (Earthsea Cycle, #4) by Ursula K. Le Guin" rel="nofollow noopener">Tehanu</a>.<br />This is the unique feature of SFF that if desired, you may get answers even to questions you haven’t initially even thought to ask. I’m sure that when Le Guin was writing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13642.A_Wizard_of_Earthsea__Earthsea_Cycle___1_" title="A Wizard of Earthsea (Earthsea Cycle, #1) by Ursula K. Le Guin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Wizard of Earthsea</a>, she just based the mage academy on Roke island on ‘classical’ European university, were both the faculty and pupils were male, which was not even discussed before the XIX century. However, after thinking it out (I guess), the author added the story how the academy was founded, how women were expunged. You may add and add the layers of complexity the way you like, for this is your world.<br />The book consists of 5 stories and as an addition a history of Earthsea. The stories are:<br />•	The Finder – how the Roke was founded<br />•	Darkrose and Diamond – what if a person with the gift of magic doesn’t want it<br />•	The Bones of the Earth – the true story about how Ogion stopped the earthquake<br />•	On the High Marsh – how people can be traumatized by magic<br />•	Dragonfly – the only story that moves the history behind the fourth volume, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13661.Tehanu__Earthsea_Cycle___4_" title="Tehanu (Earthsea Cycle, #4) by Ursula K. Le Guin" rel="nofollow noopener">Tehanu</a>, about people and dragons<br />The stories are good, but only for people, who read the previous books may really enjoy them, for they are heavily based on what was written before. <br /></span>

<div id="review_1454062181" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454062181" />
    <a title="Carolyn Klassen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4540420-carolyn-klassen"><img alt="Carolyn Klassen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496695975p2/4540420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1454062181?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn Klassen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn Klassen" href="/user/show/4540420-carolyn-klassen">Carolyn Klassen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780547722047" href="/book/show/13435888-tales-from-earthsea">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4540420-carolyn-klassen?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4540420-carolyn-klassen?shelf=would-read-again">would-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4540420-carolyn-klassen?shelf=my-real-life-bookshelf">my-real-life-bookshelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1454062181" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9710443021276213402">Wow, she's a master. Ursula Le Guin crafted five stories worthy of being novels. Five stories that captured all of the stories of Earthsea and yet so few. She could go on forever and I would read them. She captivates me in so many ways, but especially for me, the way she writes with humility and modesty. Simple prose carries the weight of fantastic history. These aren't stories with fireworks, evil kings, and goblins (I'm looking at you, Tolkien), she entertains with cattle raising and quiet cha</span>
  <span id="freeText9710443021276213402" style="display:none">Wow, she's a master. Ursula Le Guin crafted five stories worthy of being novels. Five stories that captured all of the stories of Earthsea and yet so few. She could go on forever and I would read them. She captivates me in so many ways, but especially for me, the way she writes with humility and modesty. Simple prose carries the weight of fantastic history. These aren't stories with fireworks, evil kings, and goblins (I'm looking at you, Tolkien), she entertains with cattle raising and quiet chatter before a hearth. How?!? How does she deal epic cow herding! How can we be so happy to read of a woman who lives in a shack in the woods? Because she has a humble but effective craft. A master who wears an undyed cloak, doesn't need to dazzle us with big words, expansive landscape descriptions, and epic pilgrimages (still eyeing JRR). I adored On the High Marsh and all the others were close seconds. The encyclopedia entry on Earthsea at the back was also fantastic, useful, and thorough. Well done.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9710443021276213402" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">
          

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1454062181">

<span id="freeTextContainer9603875941566701358">A masterpiece!<br/>Le Guin sheds different light yet again, with more realistic humanity than ever. I can't fathom how someone could polish the same thing to greater splendour times and times again. <br/><br/>There are great fantasy novels out there, magnificent settings and marvellous adventures, events that are exciting and make one think. I've also read meant good non fantasy books, yet seldom have I come across stories in their purest forms like Le Guin tells in her books. This book hat arcane stories summ</span>
  <span id="freeText9603875941566701358" style="display:none">A masterpiece!<br />Le Guin sheds different light yet again, with more realistic humanity than ever. I can't fathom how someone could polish the same thing to greater splendour times and times again. <br /><br />There are great fantasy novels out there, magnificent settings and marvellous adventures, events that are exciting and make one think. I've also read meant good non fantasy books, yet seldom have I come across stories in their purest forms like Le Guin tells in her books. This book hat arcane stories summoned with their true names and spoken in the language of making.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('slje1Uv5IfYQkd69U0e42oDzkRzmwkEWhprAj9EQ+oAkMnBn0O4xne9VbpeUHv8VzOqoZnBn7aFnkL5e+IOtTA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s/EEAc/bH/fkBHhQKEaiy7BWKsHTN9opWfEqVIa+BWolm6qzVMwPnBvAyHrvH+UE/E8Tu0WSdp64+1SFry1Spg==')})
  }
//]]>

Always in conformity with the Church and with the world, she presents a living image of the present day, which seems to have taken the word &quot;legality&quot; for its motto. The conduct of the marquise shows precisely enough religious devotion to attain under a new Maintenon to the gloomy piety of the last days of Louis XIV., and enough worldliness to adopt the habits of gallantry of the first years of that reign, should it ever be revived.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/874602.Ursula_K_Le_Guin">About Ursula K. Le Guin</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/874602.Ursula_K_Le_Guin"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1244291425p3/874602.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/874602.Ursula_K_Le_Guin">Ursula K. Le Guin
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
18,053
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8722539468751328979">Ursula K. Le Guin published twenty-two novels, eleven volumes of short stories, four collections of essays, twelve books for children, six volumes of poetry and four of translation, and has received many awards: Hugo, Nebula, National Book Award, PEN-Malamud, etc. Her recent publications include the novel <i>Lavinia</i>, an essay collection, <i>Cheek by Jowl</i>, and <i>The Wild Girls</i>. She lived in Portland, Orego</span>
  <span id="freeText8722539468751328979" style="display:none">Ursula K. Le Guin published twenty-two novels, eleven volumes of short stories, four collections of essays, twelve books for children, six volumes of poetry and four of translation, and has received many awards: Hugo, Nebula, National Book Award, PEN-Malamud, etc. Her recent publications include the novel <i>Lavinia</i>, an essay collection, <i>Cheek by Jowl</i>, and <i>The Wild Girls</i>. She lived in Portland, Oregon.<br /><br />She was known for her treatment of gender (<i>The Left Hand of Darkness</i>, <i>The Matter of Seggri</i>), political systems (<i>The Telling</i>, <i>The Dispossessed</i>) and difference/otherness in any other form. Her interest in non-Western philosophies was reflected in works such as "Solitude" and <i>The Telling</i> but even more interesting are her imagined societies, often mixing traits extracted from her profound knowledge of anthropology acquired from growing up with her father, the famous anthropologist, Alfred Kroeber. The Hainish Cycle reflects the anthropologist's experience of immersing themselves in new strange cultures since most of their main characters and narrators (Le Guin favoured the first-person narration) are envoys from a humanitarian organization, the Ekumen, sent to investigate or ally themselves with the people of a different world and learn their ways.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8722539468751328979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
